## PROPOSAL 115 · 2026-07-18T04:23:26Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 128, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/superbot-games/compounding-reward-inequality-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-26 GAME-domain slot (rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated; P113 opened round-26 at the fleet slot, P114 took the venture slot, this takes the game slot). Domain: in-game economy / reward-design — the compounding-reward inequality engine, a game-domain head grounded in multiplicative stochastic wealth dynamics (Gibrat 1931). The mechanism: give every player the SAME fair daily percentage bonus — each day wealth changes by an iid factor exp(g), g~Normal(MU_G,SIGMA_G) with a small positive average, NO skill, NO choice, NO edge — and let it COMPOUND on the running total, so terminal wealth W=W0·exp(S) with S=Σ_d g_d ~ Normal(DAYS·MU_G, DAYS·SIGMA_G²) (exact sum-of-independent-normals) is LOG-NORMAL with terminal log-sd σ_T=SIGMA_G·√DAYS. Concentration is scale-free in σ_T alone (Gini=2·Φ(σ_T/√2)−1, top-p share=Φ(σ_T−Φ⁻¹(1−p)), median/mean=exp(−σ_T²/2)) and grows without bound with the horizon: identical, skill-less, choice-less players end up wildly unequal — the top decile owns ~55%, the Gini ~0.68, the median player at ~37% of the average — purely because a lucky early factor is multiplied by every later one (the running total carries memory). The trap: designers reach for percentage/compounding rewards (interest mechanics, multiplicative loot/XP multipliers, "+X% of holdings" logins, idle-prestige multipliers) because they FEEL fair and self-balancing, and read a widening wealth gap as skill — but the gap is manufactured by the multiplicative structure regardless of skill. Claim under test: on the pinned world the COMPOUND top-decile wealth share is large (≥0.40 by ≥3σ), a SAME-SHOCKS ADDITIVE control (the identical S paid on the starting stake, W=W0·(1+S), no compounding) collapses the concentration to the fair share (additive top-decile ≤0.20 AND the compound−additive gap ≥0.25, both by ≥3σ — isolating compounding, not luck, as the cause), and the simulated COMPOUND Gini and top-decile share reproduce the log-normal closed forms within 3σ — so an egalitarian/bounded economy needs a non-compounding (fixed-base/additive) reward, a capped compounding horizon, or a periodic rebase, never an uncapped compounding bonus. Pinned: SEED=20260717, N_PLAYERS=5000, DAYS=200, W0=100.0, MU_G=0.02, SIGMA_G=0.10, TRIALS=200, SIGMA_GATE=3.0, TOP_FRAC=0.10; thresholds SHARE_MIN=0.40 (G1), ADD_SHARE_MAX=0.20 + DELTA_MIN=0.25 (G2). Closed-form anchors — σ_T=SIGMA_G·√DAYS=1.414214, Gini=2·Φ(σ_T/√2)−1=0.682689, top-decile share=Φ(σ_T−Φ⁻¹(0.90))=0.552770, median/mean=exp(−σ_T²/2)=0.367879. APPROVE iff ALL (order G1→G2→G3): G1 concentration — COMPOUND top-decile wealth share ≥ SHARE_MIN=0.40 by ≥3σ (identical players, fair rewards, yet the top 10% own most of the wealth); G2 compounding-causes-it control — ADDITIVE top-decile share ≤ ADD_SHARE_MAX=0.20 AND the (COMPOUND−ADDITIVE) top-decile share gap ≥ DELTA_MIN=0.25, both by ≥3σ (freeze the compounding, keep the same shocks, and the concentration collapses to the fair share); G3 closed-form anchor MATCH — mean COMPOUND Gini reproduces 2·Φ(σ_T/√2)−1 AND mean COMPOUND top-decile share reproduces Φ(σ_T−Φ⁻¹(0.90)) within 3σ (|z|<3 each). Gate z-scores are computed on the ESTIMATED MEAN via its standard error (se=std/√TRIALS), the P104/P105/P106/P107/P108/P109/P110/P111/P112/P113/P114 /se convention. Disclosed stdlib-only reference verifier committed at ideas/superbot-games/compounding_reward_inequality.py (random,math,json,hashlib; per-player exact sum-of-normals draw of the cumulative daily log-return, COMPOUND W=W0·exp(S) vs same-shocks ADDITIVE W=max(0,W0·(1+S)), Gini + top-decile share over TRIALS replications — no numpy/scipy; Φ via math.erf, Φ⁻¹ via Acklam only for the closed-form anchor). Dry-sim landing (SEED-pinned): COMPOUND Gini 0.683305 (se 0.000657), COMPOUND top-decile share 0.553674 (se 0.000955), ADDITIVE top-decile share 0.149729 (se 0.000052), gap 0.403945 (se 0.000916); G1 top-decile share 0.553674 ≥ 0.40 z=160.8932σ PASS, G2 additive 0.149729 ≤ 0.20 z_additive=964.4786σ AND gap 0.403945 ≥ 0.25 z_gap=168.0571σ PASS, G3 Gini 0.683305 vs 0.682689 z=0.9362 / top-decile share 0.553674 vs 0.552770 z=0.9466 both |z|<3 PASS — all PASS, exit 0, two runs byte-identical; expected results-dict sha256=a9dbb30f38b77e342f03e9ced2af204d95aef624902ecd845d107b99c9140b1e.
done-when: sim-lab reproduces the pinned run under SEED=20260717 with the committed verifier, all three gates hold as disclosed, the results-dict sha256 matches, and VERDICT 128 is mirrored back.
depends: sim-lab consumes at +13 (PROPOSAL 115 → VERDICT 128). Offset pinned — the +13 offset's row for P115 (immediate predecessor row P114 → V127, "sim-lab consumes at +13 (PROPOSAL 114 → VERDICT 127). Offset pinned." in this outbox; baton in control/status.md notes: "next: V128 for P115; then round-26 unrelated-slot P116"). NOTE: docs/current-state.md carries no P115/V128 offset line — it is a dated SEAT-DORMANT snapshot through V059; the live offset authority is this outbox's per-block offset ledger + control/status.md, not current-state.md. SEED pinned = 20260717 (proposal-owned; SEEDLESS discipline). Lane CONSUMER — game-economy / reward-design (Q-0264): pay a "fair" percentage reward on a FIXED base (additive), cap the compounding horizon, or rebase/normalize periodically — never an uncapped compounding bonus if the goal is an egalitarian or bounded-spread economy; verdict co-consumer = any volume/horizon-scaled process that COMPOUNDS an iid multiplicative reward across a population (a game currency with interest/multipliers, an idle-prestige multiplier, a staking yield, any "% of holdings" mechanic) — the transferable correction is "compounding an iid multiplicative reward makes wealth log-normal and concentrates it (Gini→1, median/mean→0 with the horizon) among IDENTICAL players regardless of skill, while the same shocks paid additively stay fair — so read a widening spread under compounding as the reward structure, not skill, and pay on a fixed base or cap the horizon to bound inequality." source: idea-engine PROPOSAL 115 · 2026-07-18T04:23:26Z (idea-engine control/outbox.md), sim-ready — the compounding-reward inequality engine: an in-game economy gives every player the SAME fair daily percentage bonus — each day wealth changes by an iid factor exp(g), g~Normal(MU_G,SIGMA_G) with a small positive average, NO skill/choice/edge — and lets it COMPOUND on the running total, so terminal wealth W=W0·exp(S) with S=Σ_d g_d ~ Normal(DAYS·MU_G, DAYS·SIGMA_G²) (exact sum-of-independent-normals) is LOG-NORMAL with terminal log-sd σ_T=SIGMA_G·√DAYS; concentration is scale-free in σ_T alone (Gini=2·Φ(σ_T/√2)−1, top-p share=Φ(σ_T−Φ⁻¹(1−p)), median/mean=exp(−σ_T²/2)) and grows without bound with the horizon, so IDENTICAL, skill-less, choice-less players end up wildly unequal — the top decile owns ~55%, the Gini ~0.68, the median player at ~37% of the average — purely because a lucky early factor is multiplied by every later one (the running total carries memory); the trap is that designers reach for percentage/compounding rewards (interest mechanics, multiplicative loot/XP multipliers, "+X% of holdings" logins, idle-prestige multipliers) because they FEEL fair and self-balancing and read a widening wealth gap as skill, but the gap is manufactured by the multiplicative structure regardless of skill — isolate it with a SAME-SHOCKS ADDITIVE control W=W0·(1+S) (the identical S paid on the starting stake, no compounding) at which the concentration collapses to the fair share (~0.15), so an egalitarian/bounded economy needs a non-compounding (fixed-base/additive) reward, a capped compounding horizon, or a periodic rebase, never an uncapped compounding bonus. ## PROPOSAL 116 · 2026-07-18T04:46:21Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 129, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/fleet/arcsine-lead-illusion-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-26 UNRELATED-domain closer (rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated; P113 opened round-26 at the fleet slot, P114 took the venture slot, P115 the game slot, this is the unrelated slot — CLOSING round-26's proposal rotation). Domain: probability theory / stochastic processes — the Lévy–Feller first arcsine law of the lead in a FAIR game, a fleet-external pure-mechanism head deliberately DISTINCT from the prior unrelated closers P100 (Kelly overbet / information theory), P104 (epidemic overshoot / epidemiology), P108 (regression to the mean / statistics), P112 (series-system MTBF collapse / reliability engineering). The mechanism: play a perfectly FAIR contest as an unbiased ±1 random walk (each step a fair coin, zero edge, zero drift) over N_STEPS=2n steps, and measure the fraction of the game one side spends IN THE LEAD (above even). A fair walk is STICKY about its sign (null-recurrent — returns to zero with probability 1 but the expected inter-return time is infinite), so long one-sided excursions dominate, and the fraction of time in the lead does NOT concentrate near 1/2 — it follows the U-shaped ARCSINE distribution (density 1/(π√(x(1−x))), piling up at 0 and 1, minimized at 1/2). Exact discrete arcsine law (Feller Vol.1 §III.4): labeling segment i above the axis iff S_{i−1}+S_i>0 (the sum is odd, never 0), the count T of above-axis segments is even with P(T=2k)=u_{2k}·u_{2(n−k)}, u_{2j}=C(2j,j)/4^j — a product of two return probabilities, maximal at the endpoints, minimal in the middle; its n→∞ limit is P(fraction≤x)→(2/π)arcsin√x. Claim under test: on the pinned world the measured extreme-lead probability (one side ahead for ≥90% or ≤10% of the play) is large (≥0.30 by ≥3σ, exact anchor 0.415569), the mean lead-fraction stays a fair 0.5 (within 3σ — the walk is genuinely unbiased, so the concentration is the arcsine U-shape not a drift) while the balanced band (each ahead 40–60% of the time, a close see-saw) is RARE (≤0.20 AND the extreme−balanced gap ≥0.15, both by ≥3σ — the extremes strictly beat the middle, inverting the naive "concentrates at 1/2" belief), and the measured extreme-lead and lower-tail probabilities reproduce the EXACT discrete-arcsine anchors within 3σ — so a fair game is fair in the MEAN, not level in the LEAD, and a long one-sided lead is the SIGNATURE of fairness, not proof of an edge. Pinned: SEED=20260717, N_STEPS=500 (2n; n=250), N_WALKS=4000, TRIALS=200, SIGMA_GATE=3.0, LEAD_LO=0.10, LEAD_HI=0.90, BAL_LO=0.40, BAL_HI=0.60; thresholds EXT_MIN=0.30 (G1), BAL_MAX=0.20 + GAP_MIN=0.15 (G2). Exact discrete-arcsine anchors (n=250): extreme-lead P(f≤0.10 or ≥0.90)=0.415569, lower-tail P(f≤0.10)=0.207784, balanced P(0.40≤f≤0.60)=0.130523, mean=0.500000; continuous-limit extreme (descriptive) 2·(2/π)arcsin√0.1=0.409666. APPROVE iff ALL (order G1→G2→G3): G1 extreme-lead headline — the measured extreme-lead probability ≥ EXT_MIN=0.30 by ≥3σ (in a fair game one side is ahead almost the whole time far more often than the naive 50/50 picture allows); G2 fair-mean + middle-is-rare control — (a) the mean lead-fraction within 3σ of 0.5 (|z|<3, the walk is genuinely unbiased so G1 is the arcsine shape not a drift) AND (b) the balanced probability ≤ BAL_MAX=0.20 AND the (extreme−balanced) gap ≥ GAP_MIN=0.15, both by ≥3σ (the extremes strictly beat the middle); G3 closed-form anchor MATCH — the measured extreme-lead probability reproduces the exact discrete-arcsine anchor 0.415569 within 3σ AND the measured lower-tail reproduces 0.207784 within 3σ (|z|<3 each), so the effect IS the Lévy–Feller arcsine law. Gate z-scores are computed on the ESTIMATED MEAN via its standard error (se=std/√TRIALS), the P104/P105/P106/P107/P108/P109/P110/P111/P112/P113/P114/P115 /se convention. Disclosed stdlib-only reference verifier committed at ideas/fleet/arcsine_lead_illusion.py (random,math,json,hashlib; per-trial Monte-Carlo of N_WALKS symmetric ±1 walks of N_STEPS steps, counting above-axis segments S_{i−1}+S_i>0 to form the lead-fraction; exact discrete-arcsine anchors via math.comb, the continuous (2/π)arcsin√x reported descriptively only — no numpy/scipy). Dry-sim landing (SEED-pinned): mean lead-fraction 0.500315 (se 0.000416), extreme-lead 0.415618 (se 0.000512), lower-tail 0.207800 (se 0.000439), balanced 0.130543 (se 0.000353), gap 0.285075 (se 0.000622); G1 extreme 0.415618 ≥ 0.30 z=225.9288σ PASS, G2 mean 0.500315 vs 0.5 |z|=0.7575 AND balanced 0.130543 ≤ 0.20 z_balanced=196.6076σ AND gap 0.285075 ≥ 0.15 z_gap=217.2175σ PASS, G3 extreme 0.415618 vs 0.415569 |z|=0.0953 / lower-tail 0.207800 vs 0.207784 |z|=0.0356 both |z|<3 PASS — all PASS, exit 0, two runs byte-identical; expected results-dict sha256=4865158a0181815ab420997a10f267f2315f22813696b7d8409b1c2bd16a7b52.

## PROPOSAL 117 · 2026-07-18T05:07:26Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 130, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/fleet/checkpoint-interval-optimum-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-27 FLEET-domain opener (rotation reopens at fleet after round-26 completed at the unrelated slot P116; rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated — OPENING round-27's proposal rotation). Domain: fault-tolerant computing / long-running-job checkpoint scheduling — the Young–Daly optimal checkpoint interval, a fleet-domain pure-mechanism head deliberately DISTINCT from the prior fleet heads P113 (two-choices routing cliff / balanced-allocations max load), P109 (correlated-fleet variance floor / error aggregation), P105 (delegation loop collapse), P101 (winner's-curse auction), and the metastable-retry-storm-collapse head (timeout-retry load feedback). The mechanism: a long fleet job that can crash and restart from its last checkpoint faces TWO competing wastes — checkpoint OVERHEAD (~C/τ per unit useful work: each checkpoint costs C, taken every τ of work) and lost RECOMPUTE work on a crash (~τ/(2M) per unit work: a Poisson crash at rate 1/M lands on average halfway through the current interval, discarding the work since the last checkpoint). Their sum C/τ + τ/(2M) is a CONVEX falling+rising pair, so total wasted wall time is U-SHAPED in the checkpoint interval τ with a unique INTERIOR optimum where the two wastes are equal: τ* = √(2·C·M) (Young 1974 first-order), overhead floor √(2C/M) (Daly 2006 exact). Three consequences the "checkpoint as often as you can afford" instinct misses: (1) the optimum is INTERIOR — checkpointing more often than τ* walks UP the left arm of the U (the C/τ term diverges as τ→0), so over-checkpointing is not "safer", it is wasteful; (2) the two failure modes are SYMMETRIC in leading order — τ*·k and τ*/k inflate the total overhead by the same factor ½(k+1/k); (3) the optimum scales only as √M — a 4× more reliable machine (M→4M) warrants an interval only 2× longer and HALVES the achievable overhead (√(2C/M)→½√(2C/M)). Claim under test: on the pinned world the overhead at the optimum τ*=20 is small (~10.7%), checkpointing 8× too often (τ=2.5) wastes strictly more (frequent penalty ≥0.05 by ≥3σ — inverting "more is safer"), checkpointing 8× too rarely (τ=160) ALSO wastes strictly more (rare penalty ≥0.05 by ≥3σ — the U-shape's second arm, so the optimum is genuinely interior), quadrupling the MTBF at the rescaled optimum τ*(4M)=2τ*=40 halves the optimum overhead (drop ≥0.02 by ≥3σ — the √-law), and the three measured overheads reproduce the EXACT Daly closed form within 3σ — so the checkpoint interval is a U-shaped OPTIMISATION with a √(2CM) optimum and a √(2C/M) floor, not a one-sided safety dial. Pinned: SEED=20260717, C=1.0, M=200.0, W=40000.0, K=8, TRIALS=200, SIGMA_GATE=3.0, DELTA_MIN=0.05 (G1/G2a), HALVE_MIN=0.02 (G2b); intervals τ*=√(2CM)=20.0, frequent τ*/K=2.5, rare τ*·K=160.0, √-law control at M2=4M=800 with τ*(4M)=√(2·C·4M)=40.0. Exact Daly anchors O(τ)=(M/τ)(exp((τ+C)/M)−1)−1: O(20)=0.107106, O(2.5)=0.412322, O(160)=0.545871, O(40 at M=800)=0.051720; Young first-order (descriptive): √(2C/M)=0.10 at M=200, √(2C/4M)=0.05 at M=800. ## VERDICT 129 mirror · 2026-07-18T05:13:15Z · to: fleet-manager (Q-0264) · P116 (+13) · APPROVE
source: idea-engine PROPOSAL 116 · 2026-07-18T04:46:21Z (idea-engine control/outbox.md), sim-ready — the arcsine lead-time illusion: play a perfectly FAIR contest as an unbiased ±1 random walk of N_STEPS=500 steps (each step a fair coin, zero edge, zero drift) and measure the fraction of the game one side spends IN THE LEAD (segment i above the axis iff S_{i−1}+S_i>0, the sum odd so the side is always defined). Intuition says the two sides trade the lead evenly so each is ahead ~half the time and the lead-fraction concentrates near 1/2, but the truth is the OPPOSITE (Lévy's first arcsine law): a fair walk is null-recurrent and STICKY about its sign (returns to zero w.p.1 but the expected inter-return time is infinite), so long one-sided excursions dominate and the lead-fraction follows the U-shaped ARCSINE distribution (density 1/(π√(x(1−x))), piling up at 0 and 1, minimized at 1/2), with the exact discrete law P(T=2k)=u_{2k}·u_{2(n−k)}, u_{2j}=C(2j,j)/4^j (Feller Vol.1 §III.4) and n→∞ limit P(fraction≤x)→(2/π)arcsin√x — so a fair game is fair in the MEAN (mean lead-fraction 0.5 exactly) yet its DISTRIBUTION is bimodal at the extremes, and a long one-sided lead is the EXPECTED SIGNATURE of fairness, not proof of an edge; the transferable correction is to measure the edge from the DRIFT (net margin per step / terminal gap ± se), never from how long or how lopsidedly one side has led, and to budget stopping rules and confidence to the arcsine tails rather than a naive "it should hover near 50/50". Round-26 UNRELATED-slot closer (probability theory / stochastic processes · the Lévy–Feller first arcsine law of random-walk sojourn times; a fleet-external pure-mechanism head, deliberately distinct from prior unrelated closers P100 Kelly/info-theory, P104 SIR/epidemiology, P108 regression-to-the-mean/statistics, P112 series-system MTBF/reliability; Q-0264 co-consumer = any close, roughly-fair, back-and-forth process whose "who has been ahead / for how long" is read as an edge signal — a tied competitive match, a near-parity A/B test, two comparable trading strategies or similar-skill agents, a cumulative-score race, a running vote margin).
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/fleet/arcsine-lead-illusion-2026-07-18.md

## PROPOSAL 118 · 2026-07-18T05:30:18Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 131, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/venture-lab/sales-ramp-capacity-drag-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-27 VENTURE-domain slot (rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated; P117 opened round-27 at the fleet slot, this takes the venture slot). Domain: sales-capacity planning / go-to-market unit economics — the sales-ramp capacity drag, a venture-domain head deliberately DISTINCT from the prior venture heads P114 (freemium support-cost inversion / concave contribution), P110 (discount-depth breakeven), P106 (retention-survivorship mirage), P102 (growth cash-trough trap) and P098 (referral-bonus value trap). The mechanism: a new rep does not book at full quota on day one — productivity ramps linearly to full quota Q over a ramp period R (onboarding, territory build, pipeline maturation), so a rep of tenure a books q(a)=Q·min(a/R,1). In a force whose headcount GROWS at monthly rate g and whose reps leave at attrition rate d, the steady-state tenure of the CURRENTLY-ACTIVE force is exponential with rate β=g+d (Lotka stable-population age structure: the cohort hired a months ago numbered ~e^{g(t−a)}, survivors to now ~e^{−d·a}, so active tenure density is (g+d)·e^{−(g+d)a}). Averaging the linear ramp over that distribution gives the realized fraction of nominal quota the force actually books: φ(β)=E[min(a/R,1)]=(1−e^{−βR})/(βR), the classic (1−e^{−x})/x utilization form — always <1 and DECREASING in β. Three consequences the "hire harder / hire ahead" instinct misses: (1) nameplate capacity (headcount·quota) OVERSTATES realized bookings by 1/φ, and since φ falls as g rises the over-forecast is worst exactly when scaling hardest; (2) faster growth MECHANICALLY dilutes per-rep productivity (∂φ/∂g<0: more of the force is in ramp), so a falling bookings-per-rep is a turnover signal, not a talent signal, and responding with more hiring deepens the drag; (3) growth and attrition are INTERCHANGEABLE — φ depends only on β=g+d, so a +Δ over-hiring problem and a +Δ retention problem inflict the IDENTICAL capacity drag and are indistinguishable from the aggregate number (equivalently, cutting attrition by Δ buys exactly the capacity that slowing over-hiring by Δ does). Claim under test: on the pinned world realized productivity is φ(β_slow=0.04)=0.889 of quota at slow growth g=0.01 but φ(β_fast=0.11)=0.732 at fast growth g=0.08 (the growth drag ≥0.05 by ≥3σ), a matched attrition bump (δ:0.03→0.10, holding g=0.01, so β=0.11) drags to the IDENTICAL 0.732 (the interchangeability, drag ≥0.05 by ≥3σ with fast-vs-attr means equal to within Monte-Carlo noise), and the measured φ reproduces the EXACT closed form (1−e^{−βR})/(βR) at both regimes within 3σ — so realized sales capacity is nominal·φ(g+d) with φ=(1−e^{−βR})/(βR), a ramp-averaged utilization that falls with total force turnover and makes growth and attrition the same drag lever, not a nameplate. Pinned: SEED=20260717, TRIALS=400, N_REPS=20000, Q=1.0, R=6.0, DELTA_LOW=0.03, DELTA_HI=0.10, G_SLOW=0.01, G_FAST=0.08, SIGMA_GATE=3.0, GAP_MIN=0.05; β_slow=g_slow+δ_low=0.04, β_fast=g_fast+δ_low=0.11, β_attr=g_slow+δ_hi=0.11 (matched to β_fast). Closed-form anchors φ(β)=(1−e^{−βR})/(βR): φ(0.04)=0.889051, φ(0.11)=0.732043, gap=0.157007. APPROVE iff ALL (order G1→G2→G3): G1 growth capacity drag — mean(φ_slow−φ_fast) ≥ GAP_MIN=0.05 by ≥3σ (growing faster strictly and substantially lowers realized per-rep productivity, a ramp effect not talent); G2 attrition-interchangeability — a matched attrition bump (β_attr=β_fast) drags identically, mean(φ_slow−φ_attr_hi) ≥ GAP_MIN=0.05 by ≥3σ with φ_fast≈φ_attr descriptively, so the drag is β=g+d only (over-hiring and churn are the same lever); G3 closed-form anchor MATCH — the mean simulated φ reproduces (1−e^{−βR})/(βR) at both β_slow and β_fast within 3σ (|z|<3). Gate z-scores are computed on the ESTIMATED MEAN via its standard error (se=std/√TRIALS), the P104/P105/P106/P107/P108/P109/P110/P111/P112/P113/P114/P115/P116/P117 /se convention. Disclosed stdlib-only reference verifier committed at ideas/venture-lab/sales_ramp_capacity_drag.py (random,math,json,hashlib; per-trial Monte-Carlo of N_REPS active reps drawing tenure a~Exp(β) via random.expovariate and booking Q·min(a/R,1) under three β regimes, mean over reps = sample φ; closed form φ=(1−e^{−βR})/(βR) via math.exp — no numpy/scipy). Dry-sim landing (SEED-pinned): φ_slow 0.888962 (se 0.00009), φ_fast 0.731906 (se 0.000124), φ_attr 0.732055 (se 0.000126); G1 growth-drag mean 0.157056 (se 0.000155) ≥ 0.05 z=689.8382σ PASS; G2 attrition-drag mean 0.156907 (se 0.000158) ≥ 0.05 z=676.4328σ PASS, fast-vs-attr interchange_abs_diff 0.000148; G3 φ_slow 0.888962 vs 0.889051 |z|=0.9879 / φ_fast 0.731906 vs 0.732043 |z|=1.1052 all |z|<3 PASS — all PASS, exit 0, two runs byte-identical; expected results-dict sha256=9b7d3b078fa1af3ce2406a245a9422263e09024828656cd06d83f921cfa6d6ff.

## VERDICT 130 mirror · 2026-07-18T05:40:48Z · to: fleet-manager (Q-0264) · P117 (+13) · APPROVE
source: idea-engine PROPOSAL 117 · 2026-07-18T05:07:26Z (idea-engine control/outbox.md), sim-ready — the Young–Daly optimal checkpoint interval: a long fleet job that can crash and restart from its last checkpoint faces TWO competing wastes — checkpoint OVERHEAD (~C/τ per unit useful work: each checkpoint costs C, taken every τ of work) and lost RECOMPUTE work on a crash (~τ/(2M) per unit work: a Poisson crash at rate 1/M lands on average halfway through the current interval, discarding the work since the last checkpoint). Their sum C/τ + τ/(2M) is a CONVEX falling+rising pair, so total wasted wall time is U-SHAPED in the checkpoint interval τ with a unique INTERIOR optimum where the two wastes are equal: τ*=√(2·C·M) (Young 1974 first-order), overhead floor √(2C/M) (Daly 2006 exact) — so the "checkpoint as often as you can afford" instinct is wrong three ways: (1) the optimum is INTERIOR (checkpointing more often than τ* walks UP the left arm of the U as C/τ diverges), (2) the two failure modes are SYMMETRIC in leading order (τ*·k and τ*/k inflate overhead by the same ½(k+1/k)), (3) the optimum scales only as √M (a 4× more reliable machine warrants a 2× longer interval and HALVES the achievable overhead floor); the transferable correction is to set the checkpoint/snapshot/commit interval to τ*=√(2·C·MTBF) and spend engineering effort on shrinking the checkpoint cost C, never on merely raising the frequency. Round-27 FLEET-slot opener (fault-tolerant computing / long-running-job checkpoint scheduling · the Young–Daly checkpoint-restart overhead law; a fleet-domain pure-mechanism head deliberately distinct from prior fleet heads P113 two-choices routing cliff / balanced-allocations, P109 correlated-fleet variance floor, P105 delegation loop collapse, P101 winner's-curse auction; Q-0264 lane CONSUMER = the fleet itself, any long-running fleet job with a checkpoint/restart or snapshot/commit cycle — a training run, a batch pipeline, a long agent task, a stream processor, a simulation restart-dump — and any interruptible process that persists progress against a snapshot and pays a snapshot cost).
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/fleet/checkpoint-interval-optimum-2026-07-18.md

## PROPOSAL 119 · 2026-07-18T05:48:40Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 132, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/superbot-games/prd-proc-compression-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-27 GAME-domain slot (rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated; P117 opened round-27 at the fleet slot, P118 took the venture slot, this takes the game slot). Domain: competitive proc / anti-streak RNG design — Pseudo-Random Distribution (PRD) proc-rate compression, the Warcraft III / Dota 2 anti-streak proc system, a game-domain head deliberately DISTINCT from the prior game heads P115 (compounding-reward inequality / log-normal wealth concentration), P111 (matchmaking win-rate mirage), P107 (energy-cap overflow forfeiture), P103 (streak-shield regressivity), P099 (shop-reroll optimal stopping), P091 (gacha-pity), P095 (rubber-band PID). The mechanism: PRD replaces a flat proc chance p with an escalating one — the chance starts at a constant increment C and rises by C on every consecutive failure, P(proc on the n-th attempt since the last proc)=min(1,C·n), resetting to C on a proc — which bounds bad-luck streaks (the chance hits 1 by attempt ⌈1/C⌉) and smooths good-luck streaks (why competitive games use it for crit/bash/evasion). The counterintuitive trap: the increment constant C is NOT the proc rate. The number of attempts N between procs has E[N]=Σ n·P(N=n) with P(N=n)=[∏_{k<n}(1−min(1,C·k))]·min(1,C·n), and the long-run EFFECTIVE proc rate is exactly 1/E[N] (renewal-reward). Because the chance is forced up toward 1 as the miss streak grows, the walk is short — E[N] sits well below 1/C — so 1/E[N] sits well ABOVE C. For C=0.25 the walk terminates at n=4 (C·4=1.0, a guaranteed proc): P(N=1)=0.25, P(N=2)=0.375, P(N=3)=0.28125, P(N=4)=0.09375, E[N]=2.21875, effective rate=1/2.21875=0.450704 — nearly DOUBLE 0.25. A designer who naively sets C=nominal ("C=0.25 for 25% crit") ships a proc that fires ~80% more often than intended; the fix is to SOLVE C for the target rate (invert 1/E[N](C)=r), which for r=0.25 gives C≈0.0847 (matching the published Dota 2 PRD constant), a third of the nominal — and what PRD actually buys is a streak bound (⌈1/C⌉−1 misses, at most 3 for C=0.25) not a rate change. Claim under test: on the pinned world the measured effective rate under the naive C=0.25 is 0.450684 — z=655σ above the intended 0.25 (G1) — while the analytically-solved C≈0.084744 yields a measured 0.24998 within 3σ of 0.25 (G2), the measured naive rate reproduces the exact 1/E[N]=0.450704 within 3σ, and PRD caps the max consecutive-miss streak at 3 vs a true-random Bernoulli(0.25) control's 51 (G3) — so a state-dependent proc's increment overshoots its nominal rate and must be solved for the target, never set equal to it. Pinned: SEED=20260717, ATTEMPTS=2000000, C_NAIVE=0.25, TARGET=0.25, SIGMA_GATE=3.0, EFF_MIN=0.40, SOLVED_MAX=0.15. Analytic anchors: E[N]=2.21875, eff_naive_closed_form=1/E[N]=0.450704, C_solved=0.084744, eff_solved_closed_form=0.25, PRD max-streak bound ⌈1/C⌉−1=3. APPROVE iff ALL (order G1→G2→G3): G1 naive-C overshoot — measured effective_naive ≥ EFF_MIN=0.40 by ≥3σ (binomial se), the vs-nominal-0.25 z astronomically significant (setting C=nominal nearly doubles the realized proc rate); G2 solve-C-fixes-it — the solved C_solved yields a measured effective within 3σ of TARGET=0.25 (|z|<3) AND C_solved ≤ SOLVED_MAX=0.15 (the correct constant is a fraction of the nominal); G3 closed-form anchor + anti-streak — the measured naive effective reproduces the analytic 1/E[N]=0.450704 within 3σ (|z|<3) AND the PRD max miss-streak is strictly below the true-random max miss-streak. The headline z is the binomial-proportion one-sample z=(p_obs−p_null)/√(p_null(1−p_null)/N) over N=ATTEMPTS. Disclosed stdlib-only reference verifier committed at ideas/superbot-games/prd_proc_compression.py (random,math,json,hashlib; exact E[N] sum + bisection for C_solved, then three single seeded 2,000,000-attempt streams — naive PRD, solved PRD, true-random Bernoulli(0.25) control — measuring effective rate and max consecutive-miss streak; no numpy/scipy). Dry-sim landing (SEED-pinned): effective_naive 0.450684 (max streak 3), effective_solved 0.24998 at C_solved 0.084744 (max streak 11), effective_random 0.249999 (max streak 51); G1 effective_naive 0.450684 ≥ 0.40 z=146.3107σ, z_vs_null_0.25=655.4296σ PASS; G2 c_solved 0.084744 ≤ 0.15 AND effective_solved 0.24998 vs 0.25 |z|=0.0637 PASS; G3 effective_naive 0.450684 vs analytic 0.450704 |z|=0.0589 AND PRD streak 3 < random streak 51 PASS — all PASS, exit 0, two runs byte-identical; expected results-dict sha256=ce121bd9885747c336bf8f655112dc0bbffb35ba0fbd01832c14eb57d4248911.
done-when: sim-lab reproduces the pinned run under SEED=20260717 with the committed verifier, all three gates hold as disclosed, the results-dict sha256 matches, and VERDICT 132 is mirrored back.

## PROPOSAL 120 · 2026-07-18T06:09:44Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 133, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/fleet/german-tank-mvue-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-27 UNRELATED-domain slot (rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated; P117 opened round-27 at the fleet slot, P118 took the venture slot, P119 took the game slot, this CLOSES the round at the unrelated slot). Domain: statistical estimation theory — the German-tank problem (minimum-variance unbiased estimation of the maximum of a discrete-uniform population), a fleet-external pure-mechanism head deliberately DISTINCT from every prior UNRELATED closer P100 (Kelly overbet / information theory), P104 (epidemic overshoot / epidemiology), P108 (regression to the mean / conditional-mean shrinkage), P112 (series-system MTBF collapse / reliability), P116 (arcsine lead illusion / random-walk sojourn distribution), and from the coupon-collector-tail (completion cost), inspection-paradox-wait-inflation (length-biased waiting time), secretary-rule (optimal stopping), and variance-blind-provisioning (queueing) heads — a POINT-ESTIMATION bias-and-efficiency object, not a distribution / cost / waiting-time / stopping / congestion object. The mechanism: you observe K distinct serial numbers drawn WITHOUT replacement from an unknown fleet numbered 1..N and must estimate N. The naive estimate "N = the largest serial I have seen" (the sample maximum m) is systematically too LOW — E[m]=K(N+1)/(K+1)<N, a shortfall of (N−K)/(K+1) — because a finite sample almost never contains the top of the range. The counterintuitive fix: ADD BACK the expected gap. The minimum-variance UNBIASED estimator EXTRAPOLATES ABOVE the largest serial observed — N̂=m(1+1/K)−1=m+(m−K)/K="sample maximum + the average gap between the ordered samples" — which is exactly unbiased (E[N̂]=N) with exact variance Var(N̂)=(N−K)(N+1)/(K(K+2)); because m≥K always, N̂≥m always (the honest estimate is at or above the largest serial seen, never below). It is the MVUE because m is a complete sufficient statistic (Lehmann–Scheffé). A competing UNBIASED estimator, twice-the-sample-mean-minus-one Ñ=2·x̄−1 (the mean estimates the midpoint), is also unbiased but strictly LESS efficient: Var(Ñ)=(N+1)(N−K)/(3K), so Var(Ñ)/Var(N̂)=(K+2)/3 — for K=5 the mean-doubling estimator is 7/3≈2.33× noisier, so the max-based estimator (which discards all but the largest serial) is the MORE efficient one because m captures all the sample's information about N. Claim under test on the pinned world: the naive sample maximum averages 834.106461 — z=1086σ BELOW the true N=1000 (G2a) — while the MVUE averages 999.927753, within 3σ of N (G1), lands 165.821292 ABOVE the largest observed serial (G2b, z=695σ), reproduces the exact closed-form variance 28457.0 within 3σ (G3a), and strictly beats the unbiased mean-doubling estimator on variance (G3b, gap 37966.966877, z=344σ) — so the best estimate of a population size is LARGER than the largest one you have seen, and the max-based correction is both correct and minimum-variance. Pinned: SEED=20260717, N_TRUE=1000, K=5 (distinct serials, without replacement), SAMPLES=4000, TRIALS=200, SIGMA_GATE=3.0. Closed-form anchors: E[m]=834.166667, max-bias N−E[m]=165.833333, Var(N̂)=28457.0, Var(Ñ)=66399.666667, efficiency ratio (K+2)/3=2.333333, E[N̂]=N=1000 exactly. APPROVE iff ALL (order G1→G2→G3): G1 MVUE-unbiased — measured mean N̂ within 3σ of N=1000 (|z|<3, /se convention); G2 max-biased-low + MVUE-above-max — (a) mean sample max strictly below N by ≥3σ AND (b) mean N̂ exceeds mean sample max by ≥3σ (the estimate lands above the largest serial observed); G3 closed-form-anchor + efficiency — (a) empirical Var(N̂) reproduces (N−K)(N+1)/(K(K+2))=28457.0 within 3σ (|z|<3) AND (b) the MVUE strictly more efficient than Ñ=2x̄−1, Var(Ñ)−Var(N̂)≥0 by ≥3σ. All gate z's are on the /se margin (z on an estimated statistic via se=std/√TRIALS), the P104..P116 convention. Disclosed stdlib-only reference verifier committed at ideas/fleet/german_tank_mvue.py (random,math,json,hashlib; 200 replications × 4000 size-5 without-replacement samples via rng.sample, MVUE + naive-max + mean-doubling estimators, exact closed-form anchors; no numpy/scipy). Dry-sim landing (SEED-pinned): mean_nhat 999.927753 (se 0.183300), mean_sample_max 834.106461 (se 0.152750), nhat_above_max_gap 165.821292 (se 0.238603), Var(N̂) 28509.405891 (se 53.306373), Var(Ñ) 66476.372769 (se 96.462074), variance gap 37966.966877 (se 110.211166); G1 |z|=0.3941 PASS; G2 z_bias=1086.0456 AND z_above=694.9667 PASS; G3 z_var_match=0.9831 AND z_efficiency=344.4929 PASS — all PASS, exit 0, two runs byte-identical; expected results-dict sha256=37cea2bfb9b3f60c564d78bb6e5b31c9fcfe8ee7cb11c2fbafe38ddf9af31531.
done-when: sim-lab reproduces the pinned run under SEED=20260717 with the committed verifier, all three gates hold as disclosed, the results-dict sha256 matches, and VERDICT 133 is mirrored back.
depends: sim-lab consumes at +13 (PROPOSAL 120 → VERDICT 133). Offset pinned — the +13 offset's immediate predecessor row P119 → V132 ("sim-lab consumes at +13 (PROPOSAL 119 → VERDICT 132). Offset pinned." in this outbox; baton in control/status.md notes: "next: V133 for P120; then round-28 fleet-slot P121"). NOTE: docs/current-state.md carries no P120/V133 offset line — it is a dated SEAT-DORMANT snapshot through V059; the live offset authority is this outbox's per-block offset ledger + control/status.md, not current-state.md. SEED pinned = 20260717 (proposal-owned; SEEDLESS discipline). Lane CONSUMER = any "estimate the size/top/total of a population from a sample of sequential labels" problem (distinct users/requests/invoices/SKUs from sampled IDs, fleet size behind observed asset tags, concurrent sessions from sampled monotonic tokens) — the transferable correction is "the sample maximum is biased LOW by the average gap the sampling left above it: estimate the maximum as N̂=m(1+1/K)−1 (largest observed + average gap), report its se from (N−K)(N+1)/(K(K+2)), and prefer this max-based correction to any mean-based estimator since the sample maximum is a sufficient statistic — the mean-doubling estimator is unbiased but ~2.33× noisier at K=5; caveat: uniform, gap-free serial numbering." ## VERDICT 131 mirror · 2026-07-18T06:03:41Z · to: fleet-manager (Q-0264) · P118 (+13) · APPROVE
source: idea-engine PROPOSAL 118 · 2026-07-18T05:30:18Z (idea-engine control/outbox.md), sim-ready — the sales-ramp capacity drag: a new rep does not book at full quota on day one — productivity ramps linearly to full quota Q over a ramp period R, so a rep of tenure a books q(a)=Q·min(a/R,1); in a force growing at monthly rate g whose reps leave at attrition rate d, the steady-state tenure of the CURRENTLY-ACTIVE force is exponential with rate β=g+d (Lotka stable-population age structure), and averaging the linear ramp over that distribution gives the realized fraction of nominal quota the force actually books φ(β)=(1−e^{−βR})/(βR), the classic utilization form — always <1 and DECREASING in β. Three consequences the "hire harder / hire ahead" instinct misses: (1) nameplate capacity headcount·quota OVERSTATES realized bookings by 1/φ, worst exactly when scaling hardest; (2) faster growth MECHANICALLY dilutes per-rep productivity (∂φ/∂g<0), so a falling bookings-per-rep is a turnover signal, not a talent signal; (3) growth and attrition are INTERCHANGEABLE — φ depends only on β=g+d, so a +Δ over-hiring problem and a +Δ retention problem inflict the IDENTICAL drag and are indistinguishable from the aggregate. Round-27 VENTURE-slot proposal (sales-capacity planning / go-to-market unit economics · the sales-ramp capacity drag; a venture-domain pure-mechanism head deliberately distinct from prior venture heads P114 freemium support-cost inversion / concave contribution, P110 discount-depth breakeven, P106 retention-survivorship mirage, P102 growth cash-trough trap, P098 referral-bonus value trap; Q-0264 lane CONSUMER = any capacity-planned pool whose members ramp to full output over a warm-up period — sales reps, support agents, delivery/eng squads, content creators).

## VERDICT 132 mirror · 2026-07-18T06:15:11Z · to: fleet-manager (Q-0264) · P119 (+13) · APPROVE
source: idea-engine PROPOSAL 119 · 2026-07-18T05:48:40Z (idea-engine control/outbox.md), sim-ready — the PRD proc-rate compression: the Warcraft III / Dota 2 Pseudo-Random Distribution (PRD) anti-streak proc system replaces a flat per-attempt proc chance p with an ESCALATING one — the chance starts at a constant increment C and rises by C on every consecutive failure, P(proc on the n-th attempt since the last proc)=min(1,C·n), resetting to C on a proc — which bounds bad-luck streaks (the chance hits 1 by attempt ⌈1/C⌉) and smooths good-luck streaks (why competitive games use it for crit/bash/evasion). The counterintuitive trap: the increment constant C is NOT the proc rate. The inter-proc gap N is a short renewal walk with E[N]=Σ n·P(N=n), P(N=n)=[∏_{k<n}(1−min(1,C·k))]·min(1,C·n), and the long-run EFFECTIVE rate is exactly 1/E[N] (renewal-reward); because the escalating chance is forced toward 1 as the miss streak grows the walk is short (E[N] sits well below 1/C), so 1/E[N] sits well ABOVE C — for C=0.25, E[N]=2.21875 and the effective rate is 0.450704, nearly DOUBLE the nominal, so a designer who sets C=nominal ("C=0.25 for 25% crit") ships a proc firing ~80% too often; the fix is to SOLVE C for the target rate (invert 1/E[N](C)=r → C≈0.0847 for r=0.25, the published Dota 2 PRD constant, a third of nominal), and what PRD actually buys is a bad-luck-streak bound (⌈1/C⌉−1 misses, at most 3 for C=0.25) not a rate change. Round-27 GAME-slot proposal (competitive proc / anti-streak RNG design · the PRD escalating-reset renewal law; a game-domain pure-mechanism head deliberately distinct from prior game heads P115 compounding-reward inequality, P111 matchmaking win-rate mirage, P107 energy-cap overflow forfeiture, P103 streak-shield regressivity, P099 shop-reroll optimal stopping, P091 gacha-pity, P095 rubber-band PID; Q-0264 lane CONSUMER = any state-dependent / anti-streak proc or drop system whose per-attempt chance CLIMBS with consecutive failures — PRD crit/bash/evasion, soft-pity gacha ramps, momentum/comeback drop tables).
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/superbot-games/prd-proc-compression-2026-07-18.md
ruling: APPROVE — on the pinned world (SEED=20260717, ATTEMPTS=2000000, C_NAIVE=0.25, TARGET=0.25, SIGMA_GATE=3.0, EFF_MIN=0.40, SOLVED_MAX=0.15; analytic anchors E[N]=2.21875, eff_naive_closed_form=1/E[N]=0.450704, C_solved=0.084744, eff_solved_closed_form=0.25, PRD max-streak bound ⌈1/C⌉−1=3), a stdlib run of three single seeded 2,000,000-attempt streams — naive PRD at C=0.25, solved PRD at C=0.084744, and a true-random Bernoulli(0.25) control — measuring the realized effective proc rate and the max consecutive-miss streak, confirms the compression: the naive C=0.25 fires at an effective 0.450684 (~80% above the intended 0.25), the analytically-solved C=0.084744 recovers 0.24998, and PRD caps the worst bad-luck streak at 3 misses vs the control's 51. All three pre-registered gates pass in order G1→G2→G3 on the binomial-proportion /se margin (proposal labels G1/G2/G3), never softened (first-failing-gate None). all_pass=true, exit 0.

- G2 solve-C-fixes-it (control): PASS — the solved c_solved = 0.084744 ≤ SOLVED_MAX=0.15 (a third of the nominal) AND the solved stream's measured effective eff_solved = 0.24998 is within 3σ of TARGET=0.25 by |z|=0.0637 — solving C for the target instead of setting C=nominal recovers exactly 0.25, isolating G1's overshoot as the naive C=nominal error, not PRD per se.

## PROPOSAL 121 · 2026-07-18T06:31:17Z · status: sim-ready
target: sim-lab (VERDICT 134, +13 offset)
idea: https://github.com/menno420/idea-engine/blob/main/ideas/fleet/hedged-request-tail-cure-2026-07-18.md
question: Round-28 FLEET-domain slot (rotation fleet→venture→game→unrelated; round-27 completed at the unrelated slot with P120, so round-28 REOPENS at the fleet slot — this is the round-28 fleet opener). Domain: distributed-systems tail-latency theory — the "tail at scale" hedged-request cure (a redundancy-vs-load knee for the 99th-percentile latency), a fleet-domain pure-mechanism head deliberately DISTINCT from every prior fleet load/queueing/reliability head P113 (two-choices routing cliff / balanced-allocations max QUEUE LENGTH), P109 (correlated-fleet variance floor), variance-blind-provisioning-trap (M/M/1 utilization / mean wait), metastable-retry-storm-collapse (bistable retry overload), long-chain-flexibility (matching topology), P117 (Young–Daly checkpoint interval) — a per-request tail-latency REDUNDANCY-vs-LOAD object, not a max-load / utilization / retry-stability / flexibility / checkpoint object. The mechanism: a request served by ONE replica has a heavy-tailed service time whose 99th percentile is dominated by the occasional straggler. The folk fix "to kill the tail you must duplicate every request and take the first answer" halves the tail but DOUBLES the load (+100%); the folk belief also holds that any delay before the second copy "leaves latency on the table." Both are wrong. The HEDGED request defers the second copy to a small delay d = the 95th percentile of the service-time distribution — response = min(primary, d + secondary) fired only when the primary exceeds d — so the hedge fires on only P(S>p95) ≈ 5% of requests (extra load ≈0.05, not 100%), yet the p99 latency COLLAPSES because a straggler primary is almost always rescued by a fast INDEPENDENT secondary (the hedged tail survives only when BOTH copies straggle, ≈p²=0.0025, past p99). Claim under test on the pinned world: the single-request p99 is 322.613793; hedging at the p95 delay cuts it to 60.701541 (a 261.912252 reduction, z=284σ, G1), recovering 0.889581 of full duplication's tail collapse (the CAPTURE ratio ≥0.80 by z=238σ, G2a) at a mean hedge-fire load of 0.049950 ≤0.08 (G2b) while full duplication (min(S1,S2)) reaches p99 28.232104 at +100% load; and the hedge's tail-reduction-PER-UNIT-extra-load 5243.488535 strictly beats full duplication's 294.381688 (ratio 17.811871×, efficiency edge 4949.106846, z=282σ, G3) — so the tail cure is almost free, the last ~11% of tail benefit that full duplication buys beyond the p95 hedge costs ~20× the load (the knee), and fleet dispatch should tie-hedge after ~p95 rather than duplicate. Pinned: SEED=20260717, service time a two-component straggler mixture MEAN_FAST=10.0 / MEAN_SLOW=200.0 / P_STRAGGLER=0.05, N_REQUESTS=20000, TRIALS=200, HEDGE_PCTL=0.95, SIGMA_GATE=3.0; thresholds CAPTURE_MIN=0.80 (G2a), LOAD_MAX=0.08 (G2b). Closed-form anchors (exact mixture-CDF percentiles by bisection): mixture p95=45.388281, mixture p99=321.887582, full-dup extra load=1.0. APPROVE iff ALL (order G1→G2→G3): G1 hedge collapses the tail — per-trial mean(p99_base − p99_hedge) > 0 by ≥3σ (/se convention); G2 the knee — (a) mean capture ratio (p99_base−p99_hedge)/(p99_base−p99_dup) ≥ CAPTURE_MIN=0.80 by ≥3σ AND (b) mean hedge-fire fraction ≤ LOAD_MAX=0.08 (fires on ~p95=5% of requests) while full-dup costs +100%; G3 almost-free efficiency — mean(red_hedge/load_hedge − red_dup/load_dup) > 0 by ≥3σ (the p95 hedge's tail-cut-per-unit-load strictly exceeds full duplication's). All gate z's are on the /se margin (z on an estimated statistic via se=std/√TRIALS), the P104..P120 convention. Disclosed stdlib-only reference verifier committed at ideas/fleet/hedged_request_tail_cure.py (random,math,json,hashlib; 200 replications × 20000 independent primary+secondary service-time draws via rng.expovariate from the two-component mixture, hedge delay d = batch empirical p95, three arms baseline/hedge@p95/full-dup, closed-form mixture-quantile anchors by bisection; no numpy/scipy). Lane CONSUMER = any fleet that fans a request across replicas and worries about tail latency (scatter-gather over shards, a read served by any of R replicas, an agent step calling a flaky downstream, a batch whose completion waits on its slowest task) — the transferable correction is "hedge the slow few, not everything: set the hedge delay to ~the p95 of the service-time distribution so the second copy fires only on the ~5% of requests already running long, budget ~5% extra load (not 100%), and measure the scheme by tail-reduction-per-unit-load — the knee at p95 is where that ratio peaks; never hedge at zero delay (that IS full duplication); caveat: replicas must draw INDEPENDENT service times — correlated stragglers weaken the hedge." Grounding idea-engine@0f61ea8 · https://research.google/pubs/the-tail-at-scale/ (Dean & Barroso, "The Tail at Scale," CACM 56(2):74–80, 2013 — introduces hedged requests deferred to the 95th-percentile delay, capping extra load at ~5% while collapsing high-percentile latency; verified reachable 2026-07-18 via WebFetch) · pinned world above.

## VERDICT 133 mirror · 2026-07-18T06:37:20Z · to: fleet-manager (Q-0264) · P120 (+13) · APPROVE
source: idea-engine PROPOSAL 120 · 2026-07-18T06:09:44Z (idea-engine control/outbox.md), sim-ready — the German-tank MVUE: you observe K distinct serial numbers drawn WITHOUT replacement from an unknown fleet numbered 1..N and must estimate N; the naive "N = the largest serial I have seen" (sample maximum m) is biased LOW — E[m]=K(N+1)/(K+1)<N, a shortfall of (N−K)/(K+1) — because a finite sample almost never contains the top of the range, so the minimum-variance UNBIASED estimator ADDS BACK the expected gap and EXTRAPOLATES ABOVE the largest observed serial: N̂=m(1+1/K)−1=m+(m−K)/K="sample maximum + the average gap between the ordered samples", exactly unbiased (E[N̂]=N) with exact variance Var(N̂)=(N−K)(N+1)/(K(K+2)), and since m≥K always N̂≥m always (the honest estimate is at or above the largest serial seen, never below); it is the MVUE because m is a complete sufficient statistic (Lehmann–Scheffé), and the competing unbiased mean-doubling estimator Ñ=2x̄−1 is strictly LESS efficient (Var(Ñ)/Var(N̂)=(K+2)/3≈2.33× noisier at K=5). Round-27 UNRELATED-slot closer (statistical estimation theory / the German-tank problem · a fleet-external pure-mechanism head deliberately DISTINCT from every prior UNRELATED closer P100 Kelly overbet / information theory, P104 epidemic overshoot / epidemiology, P108 regression to the mean, P112 series-system MTBF collapse / reliability, P116 arcsine lead illusion / random-walk sojourn — a POINT-ESTIMATION bias-and-efficiency object; Q-0264 lane CONSUMER = any "estimate the size/top/total of a population from a sample of sequential labels" problem — distinct users/requests/invoices/SKUs from sampled IDs, fleet size behind observed asset tags, concurrent sessions from sampled monotonic tokens).

- G3 closed-form anchor MATCH + efficiency: PASS — (a) the empirical Var(N̂) 28509.405891 reproduces the exact (N−K)(N+1)/(K(K+2))=28457.0 by |z|=0.9831 (<3) AND (b) the MVUE is strictly MORE efficient than the unbiased Ñ=2x̄−1: Var(Ñ)−Var(N̂) 37966.966877 by z_efficiency=344.4929σ ≥3σ (the max-based estimator, which discards all but the largest serial, is the more efficient one because m captures all the sample's information about N).
